6526</section>

6527<section id="_632">

6528<h3 id="_632_toc">

6529Histology</h3>

6530<p id="_167" tabindex="-1">

6531Distinctive histological features of UESL include intracellular hyaline globules and marked anaplasia on a mesenchymal background.[<a href="#cit/section_8.2">

65322</a>

6533] Many UESL tumors contain diverse elements of mesenchymal cell maturation, such as smooth muscle and fat. </p>

6534<p id="_633" tabindex="-1">

6535Strong clinical and histological evidence suggests that UESL can arise within preexisting mesenchymal hamartomas of the liver, which are large, benign, multicystic masses that present in the first 2 years of life.[<a href="#cit/section_8.1">

65361</a>

6537] In a report of 11 cases of UESL, 5 arose in association with mesenchymal hamartomas of the liver, and transition zones between the histologies were noted.[<a href="#cit/section_8.3">

65383</a>

6539] Many mesenchymal hamartomas of the liver have a characteristic translocation with a breakpoint at 19q13.4, and several UESLs have the same translocation.[<a href="#cit/section_8.4">

65404</a>

6541,<a href="#cit/section_8.5">

65425</a>

6543] Some UESLs arising from mesenchymal hamartomas of the liver may have complex karyotypes not involving 19q13.4.[<a href="#cit/section_8.4">

65444</a>

6545] </p>

6546</section>

6547<section id="_1889">

6548<h3 id="_1889_toc">

6549Prognosis and Prognostic Factors</h3>

6550<p id="_1890" tabindex="-1">

6551The overall survival (OS) rates of children with UESL appears to be substantially higher than 50% when combining reports, although all series are small and may have selection bias.[<a href="#cit/section_8.6">

65526</a>

6553]; [<a href="#cit/section_8.7">

65547</a>

6555-<a href="#cit/section_8.17">

655617</a>

6557][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

6558Level of evidence C1</a>

6559]</p>

6560<p id="_1891" tabindex="-1">

6561The Childhood Cancer Database, which does not provide central review of pathology or reliable details of nonsurgical treatment, reported on 103 children with UESL diagnosed between 1998 and 2012. The 5-year OS rate was 86% for all patients and 92% for those treated with combination surgery and chemotherapy. A multivariate analysis of the nonsurgical data revealed statistically significant poorer outcomes for patients with tumors larger than 15 cm. Seven of ten children who presented with metastases and ten of ten children who underwent orthotopic liver transplant survived at least 5 years, but details of their treatment were not presented.[<a href="#cit/section_8.18">

656218</a>

6563]</p>

6564</section>

6565<section id="_378">

6566<h3 id="_378_toc">

6567Treatment Options for UESL</h3>

6568<p id="_315" tabindex="-1">

6569UESL is rare. Only small series have been published regarding treatment.[<a href="#cit/section_8.19">

657019</a>

6571] </p>

6572<p id="_687" tabindex="-1">

6573Treatment options for UESL include the following:</p>

6574<div class="pdq-content-list">

6575<ul id="_688">

6576<li>

6577Surgical resection and chemotherapy.</li>

6578<li>

6579Liver transplant for unresectable tumors.</li>

6580</ul>

6581</div>

6582<p id="_689" tabindex="-1">

6583The generally accepted approach is resection of the primary tumor mass in the liver when possible.[<a href="#cit/section_8.18">

658418</a>

6585] Use of aggressive chemotherapy regimens seems to have improved the OS of patients with UESL. Neoadjuvant chemotherapy can be effective in decreasing the size of an unresectable primary tumor mass, resulting in resectability.[<a href="#cit/section_8.8">

65868</a>

6587-<a href="#cit/section_8.11">

658811</a>

6589] Most patients are treated with chemotherapy regimens used for pediatric rhabdomyosarcoma or Ewing sarcoma without cisplatin.[<a href="#cit/section_8.6">

65906</a>

6591]; [<a href="#cit/section_8.7">

65927</a>

6593-<a href="#cit/section_8.16">

659416</a>

6595,<a href="#cit/section_8.20">

659620</a>

6597][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

6598Level of evidence C1</a>

6599] </p>

6600<p id="_690" tabindex="-1">

6601Evidence (surgical resection and chemotherapy):</p>

6602<div class="pdq-content-list">

6603<ol id="_691">

6604<li>

6605The only prospective series to treat patients with UESL came from the Italian and German Soft Tissue Sarcoma Cooperative Groups. Patients were treated with conservative surgery or biopsy followed by neoadjuvant chemotherapy consisting of varying combinations of vincristine, cyclophosphamide, dactinomycin, doxorubicin, and ifosfamide. Disease evaluation, usually after four cycles of chemotherapy, was followed by second-look surgery when appropriate to try to remove residual primary tumor followed by additional and/or adjuvant chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_8.12">

660612</a>

6607]<div class="pdq-content-list">

6608<ul id="_692">

6609<li>

6610Ten of 17 patients survived in first complete remission, and one patient survived in third complete remission.</li>

6611</ul>

6612</div>

6613</li>

6614<li>

6615In a single-center retrospective report, five patients with UESL were treated with surgery and adjuvant chemotherapy consisting of vincristine, doxorubicin, cyclophosphamide, ifosfamide, and etoposide. Four patients had stage I disease, and one patient had stage II disease. One patient received abdominal radiation for tumor rupture.[<a href="#cit/section_8.17">

661617</a>

6617][<a href="/Common/PopUps/popDefinition.aspx?id=810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English" onclick="javascript:popWindow('defbyid','CDR0000810035&amp;version=HealthProfessional&amp;language=English'); return(false);">

6618Level of evidence C1</a>

6619]<div class="pdq-content-list">

6620<ul id="_902">

6621<li>

6622All patients were alive (range, 5&#8211;19 years), with event-free survival and OS rates of 100%.</li>

6623</ul>

6624</div>

6625</li>

6626</ol>

6627</div>

6628<p id="_528" tabindex="-1">

6629Liver transplant has occasionally been used to successfully treat an otherwise unresectable primary tumor.[<a href="#cit/section_8.14">

663014</a>

6631,<a href="#cit/section_8.16">

663216</a>

6633,<a href="#cit/section_8.18">

663418</a>

6635,<a href="#cit/section_8.21">

663621</a>

6637]</p>

6638</section>

6639<section id="_893">

6640<h3 id="_893_toc">

6641Treatment Options Under Clinical Evaluation for UESL</h3>

6642<p id="_894" tabindex="-1">

6643Information about National Cancer Institute (NCI)&#8211;supported clinical trials can be found on the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search">

6644NCI website</a>

6645. For information about clinical trials sponsored by other organizations, see the <a href="https://clinicaltrials.gov/" title="https://clinicaltrials.gov/">

6646ClinicalTrials.gov website</a>

6647.</p>

6648<p id="_1822" tabindex="-1">

6649The following is an example of a national and/or institutional clinical trial that is currently being conducted:</p>

6650<div class="pdq-content-list">

6651<ul id="_895">

6652<li>

6653<strong>

6654<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT03155620">

6655APEC1621 (NCT03155620)</a>

6656</strong>

6657 (Pediatric MATCH: Targeted Therapy Directed by Genetic Testing in Treating Pediatric Patients with Relapsed or Refractory Advanced Solid Tumors, Non-Hodgkin Lymphomas, or Histiocytic Disorders)<strong>

6658:</strong>

6659 NCI-COG Pediatric Molecular Analysis for Therapeutic Choice (MATCH), referred to as Pediatric MATCH, will match targeted agents with specific molecular changes identified in a patient's tumor (refractory or recurrent). Children and adolescents aged 1 to 21 years are eligible for the trial.<p id="_2417" tabindex="-1">

6660Patients with tumors that have molecular variants addressed by treatment arms included in the trial will be offered treatment on Pediatric MATCH. Additional information can be obtained on the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/nci-supported/pediatric-match" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/nci-supported/pediatric-match">

6661NCI website</a>

6662 and <a href="https://clinicaltrials.gov/ct2/show/NCT03155620" title="https://clinicaltrials.gov/ct2/show/NCT03155620">

6663ClinicalTrials.gov website</a>

6664.</p>

6665

6666</li>

6667</ul>

6668</div>

6763

6764 <section id="_357">

6765

6766 <h2>

6767Infantile Choriocarcinoma of the Liver</h2>

6768

6769 <div id="_section_357" class="pdq-sections">

6770<nav class="in-this-section" role="navigation">

6771<h6>

6772In This Section</h6>

6773<ul>

6774<li>

6775<a href="#_1985_toc">

6776Diagnosis</a>

6777</li>

6778<li>

6779<a href="#_1986_toc">

6780Histology</a>

6781</li>

6782<li>

6783<a href="#_1987_toc">

6784Prognosis</a>

6785</li>

6786<li>

6787<a href="#_376_toc">

6788Treatment Options for Infantile Choriocarcinoma of the Liver</a>

6789</li>

6790<li>

6791<a href="#_1802_toc">

6792Treatment Options Under Clinical Evaluation for Infantile Choriocarcinoma of the Liver</a>

6793</li>

6794</ul>

6795</nav>

6796<p id="_358" tabindex="-1">

6797Choriocarcinoma of the liver is a very rare tumor that appears to originate in the placenta during gestation. It presents with a liver mass in the first few months of life. Metastasis from the placenta to maternal tissues occurs in many cases, necessitating beta-human chorionic gonadotropin (beta-hCG) testing of the mother. Infants are often unstable at diagnosis because of hemorrhage of the tumor.</p>

6798<section id="_1985">

6799<h3 id="_1985_toc">

6800Diagnosis</h3>

6801<p id="_1892" tabindex="-1">

6802 Clinical diagnosis may be made without biopsy on the basis of tumor imaging of the liver associated with extremely high serum beta-hCG levels and normal alpha-fetoprotein (AFP) levels for age.[<a href="#cit/section_9.1">

68031</a>

6804]</p>

6805</section>

6806<section id="_1986">

6807<h3 id="_1986_toc">

6808Histology</h3>

6809<p id="_502" tabindex="-1">

6810Cytotrophoblasts and syncytiotrophoblasts are both present. The former are closely packed nests of medium-sized cells with clear cytoplasm, distinct cell margins, and vesicular nuclei. The latter are very large, multinucleated syncytia formed from the cytotrophoblasts.[<a href="#cit/section_9.2">

68112</a>

6812]</p>

6813</section>

6814<section id="_1987">

6815<h3 id="_1987_toc">

6816Prognosis</h3>

6817<p id="_1984" tabindex="-1">

6818The prognosis of patients with infantile choriocarcinoma of the liver is often poor because of the instability at presentation from hemorrhage. A 2017 case report and literature review found 32 case reports, with 6 long-term survivors. The authors emphasized the opportunity for early diagnosis and treatment of this very chemosensitive tumor.[<a href="#cit/section_9.3">

68193</a>

6820] </p>

6821</section>

6822<section id="_376">

6823<h3 id="_376_toc">

6824Treatment Options for Infantile Choriocarcinoma of the Liver</h3>

6825<p id="_693" tabindex="-1">

6826Treatment options for infantile choriocarcinoma of the liver include the following:</p>

6827<div class="pdq-content-list">

6828<ol id="_694">

6829<li>

6830Surgical resection.[<a href="#cit/section_9.1">

68311</a>

6832]</li>

6833<li>

6834Chemotherapy followed by surgical resection.</li>

6835<li>

6836Chemotherapy followed by liver transplant.</li>

6837</ol>

6838</div>

6839<p id="_412" tabindex="-1">

6840Initial surgical removal of the tumor mass may be difficult because of its friability and hemorrhagic tendency. Surgical removal of the primary tumor is often performed after neoadjuvant chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_9.1">

68411</a>

6842]</p>

6843<p id="_362" tabindex="-1">

6844Maternal gestational trophoblastic tumors are exquisitely sensitive to methotrexate, and many women, including those with distant metastases, are cured with single-agent chemotherapy. Maternal and infantile choriocarcinoma both come from the same placental malignancy. The combination of cisplatin, etoposide, and bleomycin, as used in other pediatric germ cell tumors, has been effective in some patients and is followed by resection of the residual mass. Use of neoadjuvant methotrexate in infantile choriocarcinoma, although often resulting in a response, has not been uniformly successful.[<a href="#cit/section_9.1">

68451</a>

6846] </p>

6847<p id="_1993" tabindex="-1">

6848A case report of neoadjuvant chemotherapy followed by successful liver transplant highlights the opportunity for this therapy in children whose tumors remain unresectable after chemotherapy.[<a href="#cit/section_9.4">

68494</a>

6850]</p>

6851</section>

6852<section id="_1802">

6853<h3 id="_1802_toc">

6854Treatment Options Under Clinical Evaluation for Infantile Choriocarcinoma of the Liver</h3>

6855<p id="_1803" tabindex="-1">

6856Information about National Cancer Institute (NCI)&#8211;supported clinical trials can be found on the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search">

6857NCI website</a>

6858. For information about clinical trials sponsored by other organizations, see the <a href="https://clinicaltrials.gov/" title="https://clinicaltrials.gov/">

6859ClinicalTrials.gov website</a>

6860.</p>

6861<p id="_1823" tabindex="-1">

6862The following is an example of a national and/or institutional clinical trial that is currently being conducted:</p>

6863<div class="pdq-content-list">

6864<ul id="_1804">

6865<li>

6866<strong>

6867<a href="/clinicaltrials/NCT03155620">

6868APEC1621 (NCT03155620)</a>

6869</strong>

6870 (Pediatric MATCH: Targeted Therapy Directed by Genetic Testing in Treating Pediatric Patients with Relapsed or Refractory Advanced Solid Tumors, Non-Hodgkin Lymphomas, or Histiocytic Disorders)<strong>

6871:</strong>

6872 NCI-COG Pediatric Molecular Analysis for Therapeutic Choice (MATCH), referred to as Pediatric MATCH, will match targeted agents with specific molecular changes identified in a patient's tumor (refractory or recurrent). Children and adolescents aged 1 to 21 years are eligible for the trial.<p id="_2418" tabindex="-1">

6873Patients with tumors that have molecular variants addressed by treatment arms included in the trial will be offered treatment on Pediatric MATCH. Additional information can be obtained on the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/nci-supported/pediatric-match" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/nci-supported/pediatric-match">

6874NCI website</a>

6875 and <a href="https://clinicaltrials.gov/ct2/show/NCT03155620" title="https://clinicaltrials.gov/ct2/show/NCT03155620">

6876ClinicalTrials.gov website</a>

6877.</p>

6878

6879</li>

6880</ul>

6881</div>

6882</section>

6904

6905 <section id="_934">

6906

6907 <h2>

6908Vascular Liver Tumors</h2>

6909

6910 <div id="_section_934" class="pdq-sections">

6911<p id="_935" tabindex="-1">

6912Careful attention to the clinical history, physical exam, laboratory evaluation, and radiological imaging is essential for an appropriate diagnosis of vascular liver tumors. If there is any doubt about the accuracy of the diagnosis, a biopsy should be performed.</p>

6913<p id="_936" tabindex="-1">

6914The different diagnoses of vascular tumors of the liver include the following:</p>

6915<div class="pdq-content-list">

6916<ul id="_937">

6917<li>

6918Benign tumors.<div class="pdq-content-list">

6919<ul id="_938">

6920<li>

6921Focal congenital hemangiomas. For more information, see the <a href="/types/soft-tissue-sarcoma/hp/child-vascular-tumors-treatment-pdq#_131">

6922Congenital Hemangiomas</a>

6923 section in Childhood Vascular Tumors Treatment.</li>

6924<li>

6925Multiple or diffuse infantile hemangiomas. For more information, see the <a href="/types/soft-tissue-sarcoma/hp/child-vascular-tumors-treatment-pdq#_9">

6926Infantile Hemangioma</a>

6927 section in Childhood Vascular Tumors Treatment.</li>

6928</ul>

6929</div>

6930</li>

6931<li>

6932Malignant tumors.<div class="pdq-content-list">

6933<ul id="_939">

6934<li>

6935Epithelioid hemangioendothelioma. For more information, see the <a href="/types/soft-tissue-sarcoma/hp/child-vascular-tumors-treatment-pdq#_191">

6936Epithelioid Hemangioendothelioma</a>

6937 section in Childhood Vascular Tumors Treatment.</li>

6938<li>

6939Angiosarcoma. For more information, see the <a href="/types/soft-tissue-sarcoma/hp/child-vascular-tumors-treatment-pdq#_192">

6940Angiosarcoma</a>

6941 section in Childhood Vascular Tumors Treatment.</li>

6942</ul>

6943</div>

6944</li>

6945</ul>

6946</div>

6947</div>

6948

6949 </section>

6950

6955 <h2>

6956Current Clinical Trials</h2>

6957

6958 <div id="_section_TopTrialSearch_sid_11" class="pdq-sections">

6959<p id="_TopTrialSearch_22" tabindex="-1">

6960Use our <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/search/advanced">

6961advanced clinical trial search</a>

6962 to find NCI-supported cancer clinical trials that are now enrolling patients. The search can be narrowed by location of the trial, type of treatment, name of the drug, and other criteria. <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/treatment/clinical-trials/">

6963General information</a>

6964 about clinical trials is also available.</p>

6977<p id="_93" tabindex="-1">

6978The PDQ cancer information summaries are reviewed regularly and updated as

6979new information becomes available. This section describes the latest

6980changes made to this summary as of the date above.</p>

6981<p id="_2445" tabindex="-1">

6984This summary is written and maintained by the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/pediatric-treatment" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/pediatric-treatment">

6985PDQ Pediatric Treatment Editorial Board</a>

6986, which is

6987editorially independent of NCI. The summary reflects an independent review of

6988the literature and does not represent a policy statement of NCI or NIH. More

6989information about summary policies and the role of the PDQ Editorial Boards in

6990maintaining the PDQ summaries can be found on the <a href="/types/liver/hp/child-liver-treatment-pdq#_AboutThis_1">

6991About This PDQ Summary</a>

6992 and <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq">

6994 pages.

7001

7002 <section id="_AboutThis_1">

7003

7004 <h2>

7005About This PDQ Summary</h2>

7006

7007 <div id="_section_AboutThis_1" class="pdq-sections">

7008<section id="_AboutThis_2">

7009<h3 id="_AboutThis_2_toc">

7010Purpose of This Summary</h3>

7011<p id="_AboutThis_3" tabindex="-1">

7012This PDQ cancer information summary for health professionals provides comprehensive, peer-reviewed, evidence-based information about the treatment of childhood liver cancer. It is intended as a resource to inform and assist clinicians in the care of their patients. It does not provide formal guidelines or recommendations for making health care decisions.</p>

7013</section>

7014<section id="_AboutThis_4">

7015<h3 id="_AboutThis_4_toc">

7016Reviewers and Updates</h3>

7017<p id="_AboutThis_5" tabindex="-1">

7018This summary is reviewed regularly and updated as necessary by the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/pediatric-treatment" title="https://www.cancer.gov/publications/pdq/editorial-boards/pediatric-treatment">

7019PDQ Pediatric Treatment Editorial Board</a>

7020, which is editorially independent of the National Cancer Institute (NCI). The summary reflects an independent review of the literature and does not represent a policy statement of NCI or the National Institutes of Health (NIH).</p>

7021<p id="_AboutThis_22" tabindex="-1">

7022 Board members review recently published articles each month to determine whether an article should:</p>

7023<div class="pdq-content-list">

7024<ul id="_AboutThis_6">

7025<li>

7026be discussed at a meeting,</li>

7027<li>

7028be cited with text, or</li>

7029<li>

7030replace or update an existing article that is already cited.</li>

7031</ul>

7032</div>

7033<p id="_AboutThis_7" tabindex="-1">

7034Changes to the summaries are made through a consensus process in which Board members evaluate the strength of the evidence in the published articles and determine how the article should be included in the summary.</p>

7035<p id="" tabindex="-1">

7036The lead reviewers for Childhood Liver Cancer Treatment are:</p>

7037<div class="pdq-content-list">

7038<ul id="">

7039<li>

7040Denise Adams, MD (Children's Hospital Boston)</li>

7041<li>

7042Andrea A. Hayes-Dixon, MD, FACS, FAAP (Howard University)</li>

7043<li>

7044Karen J. Marcus, MD, FACR (Dana-Farber Cancer Institute/Boston Children's Hospital)</li>

7045<li>

7046Thomas A. Olson, MD (Aflac Cancer and Blood Disorders Center of Children's Healthcare of Atlanta - Egleston Campus)</li>

7047<li>

7048Michael V. Ortiz, MD (Memorial Sloan Kettering Cancer Center)</li>

7049<li>

7050Stephen J. Shochat, MD (St. Jude Children's Research Hospital)</li>

7051</ul>

7052</div>

7053<p id="_AboutThis_9" tabindex="-1">

7054Any comments or questions about the summary content should be submitted to Cancer.gov through the NCI website's <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us" title="https://www.cancer.gov/contact/email-us">

7055Email Us</a>

7056. Do not contact the individual Board Members with questions or comments about the summaries. Board members will not respond to individual inquiries.</p>

7057</section>

7058<section id="_AboutThis_10">

7059<h3 id="_AboutThis_10_toc">

7060Levels of Evidence</h3>

7061<p id="_AboutThis_11" tabindex="-1">

7062Some of the reference citations in this summary are accompanied by a level-of-evidence designation. These designations are intended to help readers assess the strength of the evidence supporting the use of specific interventions or approaches. The PDQ Pediatric Treatment Editorial Board uses a <a href="/publications/pdq/levels-evidence/treatment">

7063formal evidence ranking system</a>

7064 in developing its level-of-evidence designations.</p>

7065</section>

7066<section id="_AboutThis_12">

7067<h3 id="_AboutThis_12_toc">

7068Permission to Use This Summary</h3>

7069<p id="_AboutThis_13" tabindex="-1">

7070PDQ is a registered trademark. Although the content of PDQ documents can be used freely as text, it cannot be identified as an NCI PDQ cancer information summary unless it is presented in its entirety and is regularly updated. However, an author would be permitted to write a sentence such as &#8220;NCI&#8217;s PDQ cancer information summary about breast cancer prevention states the risks succinctly: [include excerpt from the summary].&#8221;</p>

7071<p id="_AboutThis_14" tabindex="-1">

7072The preferred citation for this PDQ summary is:</p>

7073<p id="_AboutThis_15" tabindex="-1">

7074PDQ&#174; Pediatric Treatment Editorial Board. PDQ Childhood Liver Cancer Treatment. Bethesda, MD: National Cancer Institute. Updated &lt;MM/DD/YYYY&gt;. Available at: <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/types/liver/hp/child-liver-treatment-pdq" title="https://www.cancer.gov/types/liver/hp/child-liver-treatment-pdq">

7075https://www.cancer.gov/types/liver/hp/child-liver-treatment-pdq</a>

7076. Accessed &lt;MM/DD/YYYY&gt;. [PMID: 26389232]</p>

7077<p id="_AboutThis_16" tabindex="-1">

7078Images in this summary are used with permission of the author(s), artist, and/or publisher for use within the PDQ summaries only. Permission to use images outside the context of PDQ information must be obtained from the owner(s) and cannot be granted by the National Cancer Institute. Information about using the illustrations in this summary, along with many other cancer-related images, is available in <a href="https://visualsonline.cancer.gov/" title="https://visualsonline.cancer.gov/">

7079Visuals Online</a>

7080, a collection of over 2,000 scientific images.

More information on insurance coverage is available on Cancer.gov on the <a href="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/managing-care" title="https://www.cancer.gov/about-cancer/managing-care">

7089Managing Cancer Care</a>

7090 page.</p>
